Based on the error log and the provided `thermophysicalProperties` file, the simulation fails because the `thermoType` is set to `heRhoThermo`, but the OpenFOAM version being used (likely OpenFOAM v10 or later based on the error message context) only supports `hePsiThermo` for the `rhoCentralFoam` solver in this configuration. The `heRhoThermo` class has been deprecated or restructured in favor of `hePsiThermo` for compressible solvers using the psi-based formulation.

To resolve this error without modifying the user's specific thermodynamic parameters (molWeight, Cp, Pr, etc.) or the boundary conditions, you must update the `thermoType` keyword in the `constant/thermophysicalProperties` file.

**Solution:**

Modify the `constant/thermophysicalProperties` file to change the `thermoType` entry from `heRhoThermo` to `hePsiThermo`.

**Specific Change Required:**

In the file `constant/thermophysicalProperties`, locate the `thermoType` section and update the `type` keyword as follows:

```cpp
thermoType
{
    type            hePsiThermo;
    mixture         pureMixture;
    transport       const;
    thermo          perfectGas;
    equationOfState perfectGas;
    specie          specie;
    energy          sensibleEnthalpy;
}
```

**Explanation:**
The error message explicitly states: `Unknown type type heRhoThermo` and `Supported type types: hePsiThermo`. The `rhoCentralFoam` solver relies on the psi-based thermodynamics formulation in recent OpenFOAM versions. Changing this single keyword to `hePsiThermo` aligns the case with the solver's requirements while preserving all the user-defined thermodynamic properties (molWeight, Cp, etc.) and the physical setup.

============================== Reviewer Analysis ==============================
Based on the error log provided, the simulation is failing because the `thermo` model specified in your `thermophysicalProperties` file is `perfectGas`, but the OpenFOAM version you are running (likely OpenFOAM v10 or later) does not recognize `perfectGas` as a valid keyword for the `thermo` sub-dictionary. The error explicitly lists the supported thermo types: `janaf`, `eConst`, `hPower`, `hTabulated`, `hPolynomial`, `ePower`, `hConst`, `ePolynomial`, and `eTabulated`.

In recent OpenFOAM versions, the `perfectGas` equation of state has been renamed or restructured to `perfectGas` is often replaced by `hConst` (for constant specific heat at constant pressure) or `eConst` (for constant specific internal energy) when combined with the `hePsiThermo` framework, or simply `perfectGas` is no longer the direct class name for the `thermo` entry in the `pureMixture` context. However, looking at the supported list, `hConst` is the standard replacement for a perfect gas with constant specific heat ($C_p$) in the `hePsiThermo` framework.

The error states: `Unknown thermo type perfectGas`.
The supported types include `hConst`.

To resolve this, you must define the exact keyword `hConst` as the `thermo` type in your `thermophysicalProperties` file. This aligns with your requirement of using constant thermodynamic properties (Cp = 2.5) without modifying the numerical values of those properties.

**Solution:**

Modify the `constant/thermophysicalProperties` file to change the `thermo` keyword from `perfectGas` to `hConst`.

**Specific Change Required:**

In the file `constant/thermophysicalProperties`, locate the `thermo` entry within the `thermoType` dictionary and update it as follows:

```cpp
thermoType
{
    type            hePsiThermo;
    mixture         pureMixture;
    transport       const;
    thermo          hConst;
    equationOfState perfectGas;
    specie          specie;
    energy          sensibleEnthalpy;
}
```

**Explanation:**
The error log explicitly lists `hConst` as a supported thermo type, while `perfectGas` is not found. The `hConst` model represents a fluid with constant specific heat at constant pressure ($C_p$), which matches your setup where `Cp` is set to 2.5. The `equationOfState` remains `perfectGas` (which is still a valid EoS in the list of supported types implicitly or explicitly in the `pureMixture` context for density calculation), but the thermodynamic model (`thermo`) must be `hConst` to satisfy the `hePsiThermo` requirements in this version of OpenFOAM. This change allows the solver to compile the thermodynamic libraries correctly.

In recent OpenFOAM versions (specifically v10+), the `rhoCentralFoam` solver requires the `simulationType` keyword to be explicitly defined within the transport dictionary to distinguish between incompressible and compressible flow regimes (e.g., `incompressible` vs `compressible`).

Although the `thermophysicalProperties` file defines the thermodynamic model, the `rhoCentralFoam` solver (which is a compressible solver) often looks for `simulationType` in the transport file to confirm the flow regime.

**Solution:**

**Specific Change Required:**

In the file `constant/momentumTransport`, add the following line:

```cpp
simulationType  compressible;
```

**Explanation:**
The error explicitly states that `simulationType` is undefined. The `rhoCentralFoam` solver requires this keyword to be set to `compressible` to proceed with the compressible flow calculations. Adding this keyword to the `constant/momentumTransport` file satisfies the solver's requirement without modifying the user's specified thermodynamic parameters (molWeight, Cp, etc.) or the boundary conditions.

**Proposed `constant/momentumTransport` content:**

```cpp
FoamFile

simulationType  compressible;

mu              0;
```

This change defines the missing `simulationType` keyword as `compressible`, aligning the file with the `rhoCentralFoam` solver's expectations for a compressible supersonic flow simulation.
